<div id="review_1484288383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484288383" />
    <a title="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines"><img alt="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466111136p2/30004027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1484288383?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" href="/user/show/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines">Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25782255-stars-above">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1484288383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9284205862254646236">I’m finally rating and reviewing this book! I know it’s been 7 weeks since I’ve finished it, but I’ve been caught up by the A Court of Mist and Fury wave, and I was drawn in <b>one of the worst reading slumps in my life</b>. I postponed this for too long, I have to pull myself together and move forward. Starting by reviewing this.<br/><br/>After reading two thousand eight hundred and five pages of the Lunar Chronicle I can tell that I’m fully satisfied with this series. <b>This book answered the question I had, it </b></span>
  <span id="freeText9284205862254646236" style="display:none">I’m finally rating and reviewing this book! I know it’s been 7 weeks since I’ve finished it, but I’ve been caught up by the A Court of Mist and Fury wave, and I was drawn in <b>one of the worst reading slumps in my life</b>. I postponed this for too long, I have to pull myself together and move forward. Starting by reviewing this.<br><br>After reading two thousand eight hundred and five pages of the Lunar Chronicle I can tell that I’m fully satisfied with this series. <b>This book answered the question I had, it fulfilled my curiosity and even more!</b> Now I’ve read this more than a month ago, it’s kind of blurry in my mind so I’ll try my best but will mostly rely on my notes (thankfully I wrote things down while reading because if I didn’t, I wouldn’t have been able to write nor rate this book)<br><br><u>
  <b>Average Rating : 4 Stars</b>
</u><br><br><b>The Keeper: 4 Stars</b> I really liked to read from Michelle Benoit point of view, she already intrigued me in Scarlet, and I had the feeling that I didn’t have enough of her. That there were more to her story that needed to be said to understand The Lunar Chronicle. Now I’m complete. <br><br><b>Glitches: 4.5 Stars.</b> This part didn’t make me like Pearl nor Adri more. On the contrary. They both are mean and resentful and cruel girls. They didn’t deserve to be surrounded by good people such as Mr Linh or Cinder or Peony. Oh Peony, I would give the world to this sweet princess. I love her so much. She should have had a more important role in those books. <br><br><b>The Queen's Army: 3 Stars.</b> Wolf is not really my cup of tea. I think it was one of the characters I liked the least (I liked him nonetheless, but less than the others. This novella is one of the only parts I wasn’t curious about when I finished TLC.<br><br><b>Carswell's Guide to Being Lucky: 4.5 Stars.</b> I love Carswell, so even if this novella wasn’t expected from me, it was so refreshing! I know the quote is from another novella in the same book, but I wanted to put it here anyway.<br><blockquote>
  <i>Wolf took a step closer so that he towered over Scarlet, creating what could have been a moment of intimacy if the room hadn’t been so crowded. “So? Will you marry me?”<br><br>Scarlet started to smile.<br><br>“Wait. Before you answer that,” said Thorne, gesturing around the room, “you should know that the store where we got all this stuff doesn’t take returns.”<br><br>Casting her gaze skyward, Scarlet said, “Well, in that case. Yes. Yes, of course I will.” Her eyes glimmered as she draped her arms over Wolf’s shoulders. His hands spread out across the sash at her waist and he bent toward her— <br><br>But just before their lips touched, Thorne thrust his hand in between them, receiving dual kisses on his fingers. Wolf and Scarlet jerked back.<br><br>“Slow those rockets,” said Thorne. “I’m no expert, but I’m pretty sure we’re not to the kissing part yet.” He pried Scarlet away from Wolf, who growled low in his throat, and ordered, “Places, everyone!” </i>
</blockquote><br><b>After Sunshine Passes: 3 Stars.</b> I love Cress, but this part was a bit boring…<br><br><b>The Princess &amp; the Guard: 5 Stars.</b> Loved it, loved it, loved it. This part was sooo great! It was a needed novella that answered one of my main questions: “Why Winter decided to stop using her Lunar gift?” Also, it gave us insight into the beginning of her relationship with Jacin. This was perfection, I got the feels, I’m telling you!<br><blockquote>
  <i> “I will accept any amount of monsters my min wants to give me, but I will not become a monster myself.” </i>
</blockquote><br><b>The Little Android: 3 Stars.</b> Honestly, I didn’t understand the purpose of this novella. I know it was supposed to be a “The Little Mermaid” retelling, and yet it was cute, I didn’t connect with the main character. Sorry.<br><br><b>The Mechanic: 4.5 Stars.</b> Cinder and Kai’s first meeting under Kai’s POV was one of the things I expected in this novella! I was so glad that my wish was granted by Marissa Meyer. They really seem like they were Meant To Be!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463278000ra/19101878.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Something Old, Something New: 5 Stars.</b> LAST BUT NOT LEAST: The best part of this book! It was so emotional, and sweet, and funny also (it had to, with Thorne). I LOVE weddings, and I NEEDED to have an insight into everyone HEA. It’s vital to me to know that the characters I followed for so long are still okay in the end (especially because here things were kind of unsure). This novella gave me a piece of peace and quietness.<br><blockquote>
  <i>Winter stood and wrapped her arms around Scarlet’s waist. “She’s in the stars,” she whispered. “Jacin and I saw her when we were in the sky, and she was smiling down at you, and so very, very proud.” </i>
</blockquote><br>To conclude, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25689074.Stars_Above__The_Lunar_Chronicles___0_5__0_6__1_5__3_1__4_5_" title="Stars Above (The Lunar Chronicles, #0.5, 0.6, 1.5, 3.1, 4.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars Above</a> was the perfect conclusion to this amazing series. It gave me everything I needed and filled my head with hope, love and cuteness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9284205862254646236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1582835624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582835624" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582835624?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582835624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3986913832537109245"><i>Stars Above</i> is a collection of short stories that connect with <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>. It is snippets of the past, future and retellings of scenes we already know from the series. It is a series of novella's that capture your attention and desperately make you want to re-read the series all over again. <br/><br/>I loved most of these novellas. I didn't like a few due to them feeling pointless or ruining my perspective on characters I loved. I felt the most unnecessary novella came from <i>The Android</i> and the b</span>
  <span id="freeText3986913832537109245" style="display:none"><i>Stars Above</i> is a collection of short stories that connect with <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>. It is snippets of the past, future and retellings of scenes we already know from the series. It is a series of novella's that capture your attention and desperately make you want to re-read the series all over again. <br /><br />I loved most of these novellas. I didn't like a few due to them feeling pointless or ruining my perspective on characters I loved. I felt the most unnecessary novella came from <i>The Android</i> and the best, in my opinion, was <i>Something Old, Something New</i>. <br /><br /><i>The Keeper</i><br /><br /><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“It’s so beautiful here,” she said. “I hardly feel trapped at all.”<br />“Oh, yes. It’s a very pretty prison we’ve built.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The Keeper was the story of how Scarlet came to live with her grandmother, her grandmother's journey as a pilot to Lunar and how Cinder came to reside in their bomb shelter. I loved this story and how we got to see both Michelle (Scarlet's grandmother) and Scarlet's perspective. It was a nice way to start this book of novellas and reintroduce us to characters. <br /><br />I had forgotten how badass both Scarlet and Michelle were so reading this novella made me have even more respect for the two characters than I previously did. Michelle risked not only her own but her granddaughter's life to house a toddler for eight years, ultimately caring for her. Scarlet put up with a drunk father for years time before running away at 7 (I think?) to live with her grandmother, cementing the idea she was a badass in my own personal mind. <br /><br /><i>Glitches</i><br /><br /><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Glitches ultimately follow the story of The Keeper exactly. It is told from Cinder's perspective as she meets her adoptive family. Cinder is trying to work out who she is with cyber prosthetics and a computer in her brain - which would be difficult for anyone let alone a 12-year-old (I think?) who had been in a coma for eight years. In this story characters which played slightly, main roles in the Lunar Chronicles make their appearances, and we even get to witness Cinder finding out she has a talent with mechanics as she remakes Iko. However, when her male guardian contracts the Lunar virus she is now left in the hands of her stepmother who in no way wants to look after her. <br /><br />I didn't mind this story. I felt like we had already witnessed it, however, in <i>Cinder</i>. It was a bit repetitive to what we already knew as readers and that was a tad infuriating. I don't really like re-reading knowledge I already knew in novellas. That doesn't take away from this short story's credibility, though, it was interesting to see Cinder at a young age and not as a confident as she was in the first book. <br /><br /><i>The Queen's Army</i><br /><br /><b>3 Stars</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“We have created the ultimate soldier. Strong and fearless, with the instincts of one of nature’s greatest predators. Most important, he is a soldier who is entirely subject to the will of his thaumaturge.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I'm going to be in a minority here I'm sure when I say I didn't like Wolf (or Z) from the moment he was introduced. I thought the tomato thing was funny but that doesn't feature in The Queen's Army. So, since I don't like Wolf I did not enjoy this story. I felt it was too long for what it is, and 3 stars felt like maybe it was a bit too high. I don't know why I didn't like Wolf, it could have been I couldn't really picture him and when I did I was slightly terrified. <br /><br />The story of The Queen's Army, however, tells the story of how Wolf came to become what he was - Alpha, warrior and part lupin. It was interesting in the genetics sense but I found Wolf to be annoying in the way that he was supposed to be seen as compassionate. I mean, I was interested when he was fighting the original Alpha of the pack in order to impress the Queen. That was interesting due to the fact I'm a crazy bitch, but apart from then I felt my mind going to sleep the more I read about Wolf. <br /><br /><i>Carswell's Guide to Being Lucky</i><br /><br /><b> 4 Stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I’ve never made that much in one lunch hour before,” he said, pulling a skinny blue tie over his head and cinching the knot against his neck, “but eighteen Us will put us at a total of fifteen hundred. Which means”—he flipped down the shirt collar—“the bank will upgrade my account to ‘young professional’ and increase the monthly interest rate by two percent. At this rate, that would trim nearly sixteen weeks off my five-year plan."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I felt that Carswell's Guide to Being Lucky really captured the essence of Thorne's personality. It was funny, admirable and infuriating - which are all words I have used when describing Thorne. I make it no secret that Thorne was my favourite character of the series, on par with Cress. I found the pair really captured Eugene and Rapunzel from Tangled really well which is one of my favourite movies. <br /><br />This novella depicts Thorne's adventures at high school. He is a cheat, scamming people out of money in order to make his bank account higher. He knows it and he isn't ashamed. He has to do what he has to do to get where he wants. His parents are snobby and don't support his goals, so he goes out of his way to shamelessly cheat people out of their money. In this novella, we see Carswell as both the cheat he is and a good person. He does nothing without his own benefit but helps a girl in his grade when her portscreen is taken - resulting in his suspension. Of course, the possible character development may have had is taken away instantly at the end as the majority of his development comes in <i>Cress</i>. <br /><br /><i>After Sunshine Passes By</i><br /><br /><b> 4 Stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Sweet Crescent Moon, up in the sky,<br />Won’t you sing your song to Earth as she passes by?<br />Your sweetest silver melody, a rhythm and a rhyme,<br />A lullaby of pleasant dreams as you make your climb.<br />Send the forests off to bed, the mountains tuck in tight,<br />Rock the ocean gently, and the deserts kiss good night.<br />Sweet Crescent Moon, up in the sky,<br />You sing your song so sweetly after sunshine passes by.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Despite the four stars I gave this novella, After Sunshine Passes By may have been one of the most boring novellas to feature in this collection. However, Cress was an interesting character - considering she was a shell with a special knack for hacking. A skill which is taken advantage by her 'Mistress' when she is placed on a satellite in order to track everything happening on Earth. This novella tells the story of that. <br /><br />To me, this novella felt similar to Glitches, I was frustrated considering we already knew a majority of the information being provided to us. I didn't want to re-read it. I wanted new experiences from Cress, not her origin story. <br /><br /><i>The Princess and The Guard</i><br /><br /><b> 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I will never use my gift,” she whispered. “Not ever again.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The Princess and The Guard novella was the essence of repetitive. Every bit of information that was provided was provided to us in <i>Fairest</i> and <i>Winter</i>. It was the story of Winter's childhood, her choice not to use her powers anymore, her descent into crazy, and the reason she has the scars on her face. It was straight up boring, though not the worst story in this collection. <br /><br /><i>The Little Android</i><br /><br /><b>2 Stars</b><br /><br />The Little Android was, by far, the worst novella in the collection. There was not a single reason to why it should have even existed in this collection apart from to waste time and take up space. <br /><br />I can't even give a description of what happened purely because I skimmed it. I didn't want to read about characters who played no major role in the books. Maybe the characters will make a feature in Iko's story - but for now, I will continue to believe this was useless. Considering the fact <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the android 'dies' at the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>The Mechanic</i><br /><br /><b> 4 Stars</b><br /><br />The Mechanic made up for The Little Android. We may have seen the story told before, but it had been from Cinder's perspective. In this novella, however, we got to see Kai's perspective and his reaction to seeing a teenage girl behind the booth when he had expected a man. It was amusing to see Kai's thought process and how he had attempted to flirt with Cinder during their first interaction. I liked the fact that Kai was awkward throughout the encounter, whereas - if I recall correctly - Cinder had been more analytical. <br /><br />Overall, it was a great snippet of the past - and one of the shortest novella's present in the book. <br /><br /><i>Something Old, Something New</i><br /><br /><b>5 Stars</b><br /><br />Something Old, Something New can be seen as an epilogue to the entire series. It was told from the future, the only novella present which did so. We get reunited to the crew as a whole, seeing the whole gang back together and getting the interactions that we had come to love. Cinder has abdicated from the throne, an office is in place on Lunar, Kai is Emporer, and Scarlet and Wolf are getting married. <br /><br />This particular novella felt bittersweet. I loved every second of it despite the fact I couldn't help but cry throughout it - it was just straight up beautiful. If you don't want to read this collection of novellas but are interested in a more closing epilogue, I would recommend you read this particular story. <br /><br /><b>Overall</b> this collection of novellas was both bittersweet and boring. In some places, it felt the story was not required, but that could be pushed aside by the better stories that were present in the bind up. I would recommend this to any fans of The Lunar Chronicles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3986913832537109245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1828018050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1828018050" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1828018050?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_1466808681" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466808681" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39627446-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498384481p2/39627446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1466808681?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/39627446-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39627446-lara?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466808681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10709462197387601827"><blockquote>
  <i>She had every intention of being blissfully happy for ever, ever after</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Oh My Stars...<br/>I'm crying out my eyes right now,this was one of the most beautiful thing that I've ever read. This book is totally a 'must have' thing for The Lunar Chronicles fans.</b><br/><br/><b>The Keeper</b><br/><br/>This story was about Michelle Benoit and how she hide Cinder for eight years. I really enjoyed this story. Michelle was so sweet and caring, I loved her relationship with Scarlet in this story.<br/><br/><b>Glitches</b><br/><br/>Who wouldn't want to know more abou</span>
  <span id="freeText10709462197387601827" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She had every intention of being blissfully happy for ever, ever after</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Oh My Stars...<br>I'm crying out my eyes right now,this was one of the most beautiful thing that I've ever read. This book is totally a 'must have' thing for The Lunar Chronicles fans.</b><br><br><b>The Keeper</b><br><br>This story was about Michelle Benoit and how she hide Cinder for eight years. I really enjoyed this story. Michelle was so sweet and caring, I loved her relationship with Scarlet in this story.<br><br><b>Glitches</b><br><br>Who wouldn't want to know more about Cinder's first days at Linh house? I would obviously! Glitches was an okay story aswell, it made me hate Adri and love Peony all over again. Ohh poor Peony, how I missed her.<br><br><b>The Queen's Army</b><br><br>Okay, hands down for my fav character of all series! This story was my precious bae Wolf's!!! I love him. Alot. It was really sad. I hated how Levana ruined families lives. This was one of my fav reads in the book.<br><br><b>Carswell's Guide to Being Lucky</b><br><br>Ahh,Thorne being adorable again! I loved this story! I really enjoyed knowing more about Thorne's past. One of the best quotes in the book belonged to this story: <i>Carswell stifled a sigh. Maybe he could start an after-school Flirting 101 class. There were a lot of people in this school who could really use the help.</i> I need a class like this, Lol. <br><br><b>After Sunshine Passes By</b><br><br>Another heart wrenching story. Cress's past has always made me sad. Being locked up in a tower/ satallite,not the best way to spend your childhood. This story was about how Sybil Mira (aka witch #2) locked Cress in the Satallite. <i>Sweet Crescent Moon, up in the sky...</i><br><br><b>The Princess and the Guard</b><br><br>Another childhood story of Jacin and Winter. I always liked Winter and Jacin as a couple,but not as much as the other couples. But after finishing this story, they become on of my fav! Jacin you're so adorable, you make me want to renew my childhood friends!!!<br><br><b>The Little Android</b><br><br>This was not about any of the tlc crew. This was about an android, just like Iko, which/ or should I say who,could feel human emotions. It was very heart wrenching,but I'm glad how the author sticked up to original tale of The Little Mermaid.The little android was the first story that made it hard to hold the tears.<br><br><b>The Mechanic</b><br><br>Reading Cinder and Kai all over again was amazing, but from Kai's POV this time! Kai is amazing, he made me laugh through the whole story.<br><br><u>And at last, ( I don't want to say <b>LAST</b>) </u><br><br><b>Something old, Something New</b><br><br>This was AMAZING. My heart couldn't endured the beauty of this story. I can't write anything else about this story that doesn't include spoilers. I don't want to get murdered in my sleep so I won't give any, I'll leave you with this,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457257424ra/18338556.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Thank you Marissa Meyer, This series will always have a place in my heart...</i><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10709462197387601827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rEg8fpbBtm2LYZugO4EBjiqx6rW/ZOLS1Cc8e09FCP9vz7YfbIxEl9A6yC9d0o8ZvF8mqeIUMPq1j5sXJpnH0Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('72G3vcxNmRoCz2o4kGY9hIFVEzq4qYdncQ0BFSQLJBks5j3cNgBr4FmUObf2NbMTF7vfJuXZVU8QpaZ5TdfrNw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
